<div id="review_163992904" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/163992904" />
    <a title="Lindsey" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/649672-lindsey"><img alt="Lindsey" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1196379960p2/649672.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/163992904?book_show_action=true">Apr 27, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Lindsey" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Lindsey" href="/user/show/649672-lindsey">Lindsey</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/649672-lindsey?shelf=love-to-be-a-hater">love-to-be-a-hater</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/649672-lindsey?shelf=just-sorta-there">just-sorta-there</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/649672-lindsey?shelf=cute">cute</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/649672-lindsey?shelf=duh">duh</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/649672-lindsey?shelf=2011">2011</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer163992904" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2781529590902158731">This book made me think... if I were a character in a generic pseudo-indie dramedy what all would happen?<br/><br/>I'm thinking I would be a slightly bitter divorcee who chain smokes and uses scathing sarcasm as a defense mechanism. Coming home would unleash a fury of hilarious down home characters who would be surprised at my current state of bitchiness but would still embrace me, slowly chipping away at my hard exterior until my slightly warmer (still bitchy) interior is exposed. Maybe my ex-husband wou</span>
  <span id="freeText2781529590902158731" style="display:none">This book made me think... if I were a character in a generic pseudo-indie dramedy what all would happen?<br /><br />I'm thinking I would be a slightly bitter divorcee who chain smokes and uses scathing sarcasm as a defense mechanism. Coming home would unleash a fury of hilarious down home characters who would be surprised at my current state of bitchiness but would still embrace me, slowly chipping away at my hard exterior until my slightly warmer (still bitchy) interior is exposed. Maybe my ex-husband would show up in some weird attempt to win me back but I'd have a really hard time with it because I ran into my old high school crush (Jake or Rambo) who is looking good and has flawless hair- making me reevaluate not going to homecoming with him and instead studying for my SATs that I got a perfect score on, allowing me to get a full scholarship somewhere prestigious and that's why I'm always quoting things and typing on a typewriter the whole time I'm home. <br /><br />Jake/Rambo would take me on a cute/romantic date. Maybe to the old roller rink or a possible haunted amusement park at night, since he knows the owner. There might even be a cool five minute Scooby Doo mystery thrown in for shits and giggles because that's the kind of hijinks we're used to, Jake/Rambo and me. Right as we're about to kiss in the Love Tunnel, something will stop us from it and the reason he is still single will be made apparent to me, either by a talking crab- his beeper going off showing he's a workaholic and/or drug user/dealer- his kid he hasn't told me about being arrested and him needing to go bail them out- etc., etc. Either way: <i>hilarious</i>.<br /><br />I'll be driving home listening to a great song that will define this movie, when something will spring in front of my car. I swerve to avoid the deer/stallion/minotaur that darted out in front of my car and find myself face to face with my ex-husband, who is laying on top of his car drinking out of a paper bag at a scenic overlook.<br /><br />We'll have a real heart to heart, establishing why things didn't work out and probably never will but we'll have some hope and longing and maybe a few minutes of some sloppy making out, since Jake/Rambo left me hanging in the Love Tunnel earlier. I'm not proud but it will establish that the door is "closed" but also open a crack.<br /><br />He'll leave and I'll look out on the scenery, that song will start playing again and I'll get a look of determination and know, forget hot ex-husband and Jake/Rambo- I can make it in this world alone. As long as I have my trusty typewriter and my abundent frequent flyer miles... since I'll be leaving for Rome the next day, setting up my next movie since this one is going to be a box office GIANT. </span>
  <a data-text-id="2781529590902158731" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('s0mMBV8ZKGri8hDfxjp9rpgcODYw01aV5XtUyGs4lPLIZDanKLMFugW2EYOL+dkVlQ9N9svCYYEbkximOn0VNg==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('rcBK93COwFQdnteB6EuqPro0UheELNpwnqlYgi8RwlLW7fBVByTthPra1t2liA6Ftycn13897WRgQRTsflRDlg==')})
  }

Many years later, one sister lives with her black daughter in the same southern town she once tried to escape. The other secretly passes for white, and her white husband knows nothing of her past. Still, even separated by so many miles and just as many lies, the fates of the twins remain intertwined.       var newTip = new Tip($('bookCover_51907346'), "\n\n  <h2><a class=\"readable bookTitle\" href=\"https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/51907346-all-adults-here?from_choice=false&amp;from_home_module=false\">All Adults Here<\/a><\/h2>\n\n      <div>\n        by <a class=\"authorName\" href=\"/author/show/1983563.Emma_Straub?a=9&amp;origin=related_works\">Emma Straub<\/a><span title=\"Goodreads Author!\">*<\/span>\n      <\/div>\n\n          <div class=\"smallText uitext darkGreyText\">\n            <span class=\"minirating\"><span class=\"stars staticStars notranslate\"><span size=\"12x12\" class=\"staticStar p10\"><\/span><span size=\"12x12\" class=\"staticStar p10\"><\/span><span size=\"12x12\" class=\"staticStar p10\"><\/span><span size=\"12x12\" class=\"staticStar p6\"><\/span><span size=\"12x12\" class=\"staticStar p0\"><\/span><\/span> 3.62 avg rating &mdash; 35,933 ratings<\/span>            &mdash; published 2020\n          <\/div>\n\n    <div class=\"addBookTipDescription\">\n      \n<span id=\"freeTextContainer18338343538287373353\">When Astrid Strick witnesses a school bus accident in the center of town, it jostles loose a repressed memory from her young parenting days decades earlier. Suddenly, Astrid realizes she was not quite the parent she thought she’d been to her three, now-grown children. But to what consequence?\n\nAstrid’s youngest son is drifting and unfocused, making parenting mistakes of his own. Her daughter is intentionally pregnant yet struggling to give up her own adolescence. And her eldest seems to measure his adult life according to standards no one else shares. But who gets to decide, so many years later, which long-ago lapses were the ones that mattered? Who decides which apologies really count? It might be that only Astrid’s thirteen-year-old granddaughter and her new friend really understand the courage it takes to tell the truth to the people you love the most.\n\nIn All Adults Here, Emma Straub’s unique alchemy of wisdom, humor, and insight come together in a deeply satisfying story about adult siblings, aging parents, high school boyfriends, middle school mean girls, the lifelong effects of birth order, and all the other things that follow us into adulthood, whether we like them to or not.<\/span>\n  <a data-text-id=\"18338343538287373353\" href=\"#\" <span id="freeTextContainer1781003722069468206"><a href='https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/26163.Jonathan_Tropper' title='Jonathan Tropper' rel='nofollow noopener'>Jonathan Tropper</a> is the author of <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/242159.Everything_Changes' title='Everything Changes' rel='nofollow noopener'>Everything Changes</a>, <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/46661.The_Book_of_Joe' title='The Book of Joe' rel='nofollow noopener'>The Book of Joe</a> , which was a Booksense selection, and <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/53849.Plan_B' title='Plan B' rel='nofollow noopener'>Plan B</a>. He lives with his wife, Elizabeth, and their children in Westchester, New York, where he teaches writing at Manhattanville College. <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/242157.How_To_Talk_To_A_Widower' title='How To Talk To A Widower' rel='nofollow noopener'>How To Talk To A Widower</a> was optioned by Paramount Pictures, and <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/242159.Everything_Changes' title='Everything Changes' rel='nofollow noopener'>Everything Changes</a> and <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/46661.The_Book_of_Joe' title='The Book of Joe' rel='nofollow noopener'>The Book of Joe</a> are also in development as feature films.<br/><br/>-Infor</span>
  <span id="freeText1781003722069468206" style="display:none"><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/26163.Jonathan_Tropper" title="Jonathan Tropper" rel="nofollow noopener">Jonathan Tropper</a> is the author of <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/242159.Everything_Changes" title="Everything Changes" rel="nofollow noopener">Everything Changes</a>, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/46661.The_Book_of_Joe" title="The Book of Joe" rel="nofollow noopener">The Book of Joe</a> , which was a Booksense selection, and <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/53849.Plan_B" title="Plan B" rel="nofollow noopener">Plan B</a>. He lives with his wife, Elizabeth, and their children in Westchester, New York, where he teaches writing at Manhattanville College. <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/242157.How_To_Talk_To_A_Widower" title="How To Talk To A Widower" rel="nofollow noopener">How To Talk To A Widower</a> was optioned by Paramount Pictures, and <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/242159.Everything_Changes" title="Everything Changes" rel="nofollow noopener">Everything Changes</a> and <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/46661.The_Book_of_Joe" title="The Book of Joe" rel="nofollow noopener">The Book of Joe</a> are also in development as feature films.<br /><br />-Information from <a href="http://www.jonathantropper.com/pages/bio.htm" rel="nofollow noopener">www.jonathantropper.com</a> </span>
